Ragacin email sent reference the solar screen.. 

For those that want to know.. Its called "COOLSHADE" the company is called RD Sunshine.  Mike is who you need to talk with $100-150 gets enough screen for one complete TIE. Remember before you order the screen used on the tie is cut for different angles. Not straight up and down so measure accrdingly.

Heres the info:

RD Sunshine Company, 611 Magic Mile Road # 201 Arlignton, TX 76011 tel: 817-459-3337  fax: 817-459-3008

Hope that helps.  I also have instructions for completing the HERO version with real screen!

Post #15  (forum post #7483)
Author    : swpropmaker
Date      : May 10, 2003 at 4:47 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

All,

Gonna chime in with my few cents worth on rhe KOOLSHADE screen.  Ive constructed two of the HERO Ties and 4' x 6'  is almost enough to do two complete TIES!  As a minimum bare any mistakes in cutting you can make ONE HERO TIE FIGHTER using 1.8' x 4.6' of KoolShade Material see pics (the screen is smaller than the size given).  I have the patterns for the hero wings.  Remember to add 1/8" to 1/4" to the pattern as it is hidden by the wing struts and Plastruct H beam.  

You will need 8 of the top piece and 16 of the other.  2'x 6' is a safe if you make alot of mistakes but if you want the amount with no left over 1.8' x 4.6'  is enough.  It easily cuts with scissors so as long as you make the pattern and work one piece at a time you'll be fine.  Get with Mark to see what that size would cost.  May safe $30 to $50 bones.  Thats enough to buy a much needed parts kit or take your lady out to dinner for putting up with this maddness! 

[IMAGE: 25060672.jpg]

[IMAGE: 25060667.jpg]

[IMAGE: 25060658.jpg]

Post #22  (forum post #10803)
Author    : swpropmaker
Date      : Dec 27, 2003 at 12:42 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

BoatBuilder,

You are correct with your observation.  You can see the Pyro being added to the wings(putty).  The wings are made of a light plastic and pre scored to allow them to break apart.  I also saw a behind the magic thingy that showed the special plastik explosive especially designed for the film industry.  Can work it like play dough.

Steve

Post #35  (forum post #11648)
Author    : swpropmaker
Date      : Mar 11, 2004 at 3:14 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hey All,

Tim's right.. Im in the process of having a very large pressure vessle constructed.  I'll be able to provide pressure castings up to 19" wide and 36" tall using degassed molds.  I had to come up with $2000 for the certified welders/fabricators to build and certify its construction.  Will the investment pay off.  ??  at least the casting will be clean! 

As far as the TIE molds go.. The wing needs to be flipped and the last side RTV poured then the molding process will be complete.  Took 80 oz of RTV on the first side pour... the same for the next. 

I should have the pressure chamber up and running in two weeks or so then the wings can be cast under pressure to ensure all the detail is super crisp and no voids are present.

I scored a 5 gallon Pressure Pot on Ebay for $150  will do all medium sized molds to include the TIE Hull. All pieces will be cast in this way.

Steve

UPDATE!! GOODNEWS.. BADNEWS

Good News first..  the TIE MOLDS ARE DONE!!!  I will be picking up my 4ft pressure chamber on Thursday castings by the weekend!  The molds look great!!  Detail is crisp..man Im stoked about this one!!

Bad news... totally destroyed the Wing master..  broke in half and three other places..  can use as wing rut masters though.. The cast screen material version... hummmm will use the first two good castings to replace the broken one...

So though really bad news the good news is parts can be of value and used.

Those that have committed will be first searved!  those that havent email me.. 

Im so happy!   Ohh the pressure chamber to deliver bubble free castings cost $3000 and its 4 ft tall  20" Diameter!  It weighs near 500 lbs!  Only the best for you guys!

Update???... did someone say update.  Here is the test pull of the center hub... white resin raw... grey with a coat of paint.  Please take a look at the crispness of the detail parts on this hub.  No mud here anywhere.  Im using a 80 gallon pressure pot to cast these solid. 

I still have to play with the slow set resin its comming out real brittle.. broke the rest of the wing taking it from the mold...  think I havent got the 1:1 by weight down yet..  they promised me it has the same qualities of easy Flo 60 the resin fawst cure i normally use.. ok enjoy the pics..

email or pm if you have any questions..

Post #41  (forum post #12066)
Author    : swpropmaker
Date      : Apr 12, 2004 at 10:59 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I know guys the wait is terrible!  I think it will be well worth it though!

Ive been in consult with the folks at POLYTEK and have determined I demolded to early.  Apparently with the cold spell that came in this weekend caused the resin to not cure..go into a dormaint state.  Once heated the curing finished and now Im in buisness!!   

This summer the shop stays at about 80-90 degrees so it wont be a problem.  Got another test run going the huge pot pressured up to 90 psi.  Some casters believe 30 to 40 psi is enough but Ive found at altitude (Denver) 80 to 90 psi  does the trick.

Heres a shot of the unpainted wing hub...

[IMAGE: 50894767.jpg]

 

Check out the pic of the HUGE pressure pot! 4.5 ft tall and 20" wide! Had it custom made!  Binks wanted $3500 for a smaller version... had this one done near $1600 bones it is certified by a prof pressure vessel maker so no worries of it exploding!  Ok maybe a little worry but Ive been told it will hold 250 PSI easy.  

[IMAGE: 50894779.jpg]

 

So if you have any Mold making or casting needs dont hesitate in asking!  I have 1 each 2.5 gallon, 5 gallon and the huge 80 gallon pressure pots to make bubble free castings of all sizes!  I also have a vaccume chamber and pump that can degass RTV to 28" of mercury to make sure a bubble free and strong mold end product.

Hope to have wing pics for you in the morning!  Wish me luck!

Steve

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hey steve...try this it migh thelp out with the mass emailing

Create a personal distribution list

On the File menu, point to New, and then click Distribution List.

In the Name box, type a name. 

The distribution list is saved in your Contacts folder by the name you give it. 

Click Select Members. In the Show names from the list, click the address book that contains the e-mail addresses you want in your distribution list. 

In the Type name or select from list box, type a name you want to include. In the list below, select the name, and then click Add. How to select multiple items.

If you want to add a longer description of the distribution list, click the Notes tab, and then type the text.

Click Save and Close. 

Hope that helps 

[IMAGE: icon_wink.gif]

Jedi Dade

I like hearing all these great ideas!  Keep em comming!  Talked with a fellow mold maker and got some new direction..

going to make a new mold for the hero wing sets.  Instead of doing each by hand from the standard molds.. Im going to do them in separate mold configured to be able to be pressure cast.

I have a idea on molding the TIE hull hollow.. hows this.. I find a steel or alluminum rod roughly the size of the wing tips and place it in the mold  paint in the resin on all the details and add enough resin to coat the entire mold as i rotate it until cured.. this would not be pressure cast but  would be hollow and have support for the heavy wings..you could also add a threaded block in the center to facilitate rear and bottom mounting....  just a thought

Steve

That sounds like it would be a good idea to maintain the strength of the tie if you wanted it hollow cast, but I think that with a solid cast and careful drilling for the cockpit, the tie would be able to support the wings without the need of a metal support going all the way through the body.  Besides, if your going to scratchbuild an interior the metal rod would cause difficulty in placement of the pilot.  However, for those that want to lessen the weight of the model it would be a perfect option.

Post #74  (forum post #14160)
Author    : wizardofflight
Date      : Sep 3, 2004 at 3:19 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I had some thoughts on how to casting a hollow Tie fuselage, this maybe over complicating  the issue, but here goes.  This uses a version the solid steel rod mentioned above, but with a twist. 

Materials needed:

1  Styrofoam ball from a craft store

2  Sections of Brass tubing

1  Steel rod sized to slip inside the brass tubing, it should be longer than the finished part.

Make a shih kabob using the steel rod as the skewer (the rod will need to be lubed to prevent it from sticking), brass tubing, styrofoam ball, brass tubing, insert this assembly in to the mold.  After casting the styrofoam ball can be dissolved with acetone or similar solvent friendly to the resin.

The brass tubing should be left a little long and the wings can be mechanically attached to the brass tubing.

Any thoughts?

Alan

Post #80  (forum post #14428)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Oct 7, 2004 at 5:37 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Awesomely nice work, Steve. As you seem open to the idea of new moulds and special versions, I have a suggestion - you could split the hull into top and bottom halves and cast hollow for people who want to do a cockpit. Depending on the setup of your existing mould, you might even be able to do this by modifying it, rather than re-moulding. (I've had some success modifying existing moulds for new pouring orientations etc - not as hard as you first think.) Advantages include lighter castings, less resin used therefore lower per-unit costs, less heat generated therefore longer mould life, etc. Strength needn't be compromised much - the cockpit ball would be plenty strong enough with a thick floor and rear wall and say 1/4" thick front/upper walls, which would still leave tons of space for a cockpit. 

Please email me if I can be any help: nipngnwm@q-net.net.au

Cheers, 

Martyn
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #81  (forum post #14429)
Author    : Nwerke
Date      : Oct 7, 2004 at 5:58 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Drat, can't edit. Meant to say "if you're interested and want to discuss modifying moulds" in the email me bit. 

Might as well go into it a little anyway. Alan's suggestion above won't work well (no offence Alan!). That technique IS used here and there, but it's tricky. I don't think it is worth using foam, especially with small or thin locating pins - too buoyant and easily dislodged, can result in off-centre castings or surface flaws. I've no idea whether it would cope with pressure-casting, also.

I think the best option is to completely divide the mould and make new half-moulds for the inner surfaces, but a good combination approach would be to create an RTV plug, to feed through from the rear hatch area and occupy the space that will become the cockpit. I mix the RTV with microballoons for these as it makes the stuff foamier, and hollow them out after they set, too. That way a spheroid plug larger than the opening it fits through can still be pulled safely from the casting. It needs to be rigid enough to hold shape, but also flex enough to get it out again - a foam ball won't do that. It's also a LOT more controllable. Note the hollowed area of the plug needs to connect to the casting chamber, or the pressure will squash it.

Happy to discuss further if you're interested.

Cheers,

Martyn

Sounds good! 

[IMAGE: icon_smile.gif]

The cockpit is hollowed out approx. 2.7 cm and the overall depth from front to back is about 10.5 cm, yielding a "net" internal resin thickness of around 8 cm. These are dims of the hull "ball" but do not include either the window frame piece or the back detail piece which are separate.

Steve isn't ripping anyone off. Then again, when people spend a huge chunk of hard-earned change on something like this and then don't get the product for a very long time, it can be very difficult to relax and remain confident that you did not just flush all that money.

I am going through this right now with not one but TWO very expensive projects (lots of money outstanding, still waiting for delivery), so I for one can relate to those who are getting fidgety. I sent Steve money for TWO kits, and I am still waiting on the final hero wing cores. 

Am I worried? NO. Steve is a stand-up guy and I am confidant he will deliver when he gets back. I will get what was promised and I know it will be worth the wait.

But I do know some other people who forked out and have received nothing at all, and I can definitely relate to how they might be feeling about it. I can't afford to lose that kind of money, and few people can.

All I can offer is the assurance from myself and others who know Steve that he is on the level. This is about circumstances beyond anyone's control, not any malfeasance. I have $$ at stake here so I have no reason to give false assurances.

For what it's worth and hope it helps. . .
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

To all concerned: I've been a good friend of Steve's for the last three years. I flew up to visit him before his deployment. He is a standup guy and he will honor all his deals. She is not involved in his projects and dealings with this board. I know for a fact that she doesn't even know his paypal or eBay passwords. I've helped him with paying his eBay fees that were overdue because of his deployment.

He doesn't have the luxury of surfing the Internet whenever he wants right now so it may take a week, or a month for him to get back to you. He is living in an environment that no one can imagine. The base he is at is attacked multiples times a day, mortars, rockets... I can't imagine this hobby crosses his mind much lately. Survival and getting back to his loved ones are his top priority right now.

Give the guy a break, he is doing all he can to come back alive, and even then, I'd suspect he'll want to spend all his time with his family before jumping back into pouring resin for us.

Post #112  (forum post #17019)
Author    : swpropmaker
Date      : Mar 26, 2005 at 6:36 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hello all, I have returned.  (Ive always wanted to say that.)

I have spent the last hour or so reading through the thread and have went back and forth with different emotions.  I guess no one knows how bad I felt about leaving folks hanging with undelivered kits.  It bothered me greatly.  Especialy when there was absolutley nothing I could do about it.  

Those of you that supported me while I was conducting combat operations in Iraq I thank you from the bottom of my heart.  reading some of the posts really made me appreciate why I fight and am a member of the armed services.  A "brotherhood" so to speak.  I Thank each and every one you all that stood with me while I was overseas.

So the burning question is when will TIE production begin.  I have the next 35 days off and nothing but time on my hands.  I am JET lagged abit but in a few days I'll be right as rain.  So starting next week I will get all the wifes crap out of my shop area and begin.

I have three phases that I will be working on at the same time. 

Phase One: Begin  sending out the kits I have that are missing two or three parts then produce three kits and have a surplus so I never take money again without being able to ship the product. I have committed to do three TIE kits a month so I should have that many on hand at any given time.

Phase two TIE Hero wing construction and molding.  I am waiting on AUTOCAD drawings of the TIE wing frame that Im having laser cut from 1/8" acrylic.   Then I will add all the kit bashed detail.  This will allow me to mold the wing stars flat on the back which will ease construction of the HERO wings using KOOL SHADE.  In that Laser cutting order they are also cutting the Studio Scale TIE Inerceptor wing prototype that I have plans on releasing in a few months.  When I left I was only missing 3 or 4 little pieces that could be easily scratched. So that is in the works.

Phase three:  Finish current Hero build up and kits that require the new molded wings and  complete all builds that I have committed to do.  Later in this phase the Interceptor will be molded and become available.  

I have committed to do three TIE kits a month so not to run into the problems I created when I left.  I have invested alot of cash to build my shop to create quality products and I will continue to do so with your support.  I will not leave anyone hanging.  I make that promise to each and eveyone of you.  

With that I would ask for each of you to email If I owe you anything.   I have a email listing I will match dates against because I have a work bench filled with several TIE builds Xwing parts here and there a few ATAT castings also and just want to make sure I am not missing anyone.  

I know it will be a little overwhelming at first making the transition from daily ground combat operations to Life, family and finally moldel making.  I fulfilled my commitment to my country now I am going to fulfill my commitment to you all and future collectors.  

I will not let you guys down.  Email me at  sneisen@comcast.net

Steve

[image]http://pic17.picturetrail.com/VOL846/454527/1306257/90570766.jpg[/image]

Post #123  (forum post #17120)
Author    : swpropmaker
Date      : Apr 2, 2005 at 7:15 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hey Guys,

Thanks for all the welcome backs.  It is indeed good to be home.  I  have been working in the shop and am proud to say we have made much progress.  In roughly two days we produced 3 kits and several extra of the small pieces.  

 I have a "resin monkey" working with me now his name is Ryan and goes by the handle RPF "Belleauwood"  We sure got alot done with two of us working.

TIE kits are ready to go. Here is what the kit comes shipped in and the contents of each box. 

[IMAGE: 91602850.jpg]

I am working on finishing the final few orders then I will start producing the 2nd run list as soon as the 1st run is taken care of.

I stopped by the Laser cutter yesterday and have found a gold mine.  I have to convert my drawing files for the Hero wing.  Then should be well on the way to finish the HERO wing build up and molds.  The process is awsome.  No more ruler scribbing fro me.   HE also took a look at the Interceptor drawig and will laser cut each layer that makes up the wing before all the detail is added.  Will save a bunch of time working on the master.

Please email me with any questions you may have.

Its GREAT to be home.

Steve

*Build up notes*  I have made contact with KOOLSHADE and it IS still available.  Also  JV, I have a drill press now and am in the process of coring your hull out.  I think it will work because of the even pressure.  I shattered two hull trying to do it by hand.  YIKES.  40 OZ resin a shot down the tubes.

Post #128  (forum post #17165)
Author    : swpropmaker

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

KK, PM sent my friend.  

JDH, not sure the size I took a hull down there and bought the closest they had without going over...  No pre drill  just shot down the back side slowly then the front.  After that  drilled the hatch opening.  Need 4 hands for the project so it was great the Ryan was there.  Need to stablize the hull without damaging detail, need to have a finger on the kill switch to catch the core once it separates and one operating the drill press.. well ok two hands for Hull stabelization.

The key is the drill press.  DO NOT try this with a hand held or your hull will dface the same fate as two previous ones.

Steve

Hey Guys,

Thanks for the support went through another barrage of tests this week and the prelim results is good.  The EKG and Stress test showed no sign of Heart damage and Ive started medication for High Blood Pressure.  I am in good shape so the doctors say i should be fine, pending the results of the blood work and other tests.  Thanks again for all your support.  I was really scared, Ive got a 15, 13 and 2 year old children and to start having heart problems at 38 really was scary.

Ive statrted poring parts again today and should be up to full speed by next week. 

I wanted to say  Thanks to Ryan who has helped me when  I couldnt do anything.  Thanks again buddy.

Guys if your waiting please hang int here.  I promise to take care of each and everyone of you.

[snapback]1126330[/snapback]​

Not a problem Steve.  Trust me, I was a little freaked out when you told me about it, NOT a good place to be. I know first hand being 29 and having a BP for the last few years that the doctors could only scratch their heads at when nothing seemed to work to get it down.  Took awhile, but its under control and has been for the past year, nothing like the doc telling ya that you've added back 20+ years of your life expectancy and for the first time in 4 years you are finally out of "imminent stroke" BP range. Feels pretty good. But, I remember thinking every day during that time that "this" day could be the one I had a freaking stroke and could be dead, or worse, a vegetable, and what I would be leaving behind, and I don't even have any kids. So, I'm super glad everythings worked out as well as it can in your circumstance.

  To everyone else, I was keeping a low profile here since I wasn't quite sure what was going to happen with Steve and quite frankly I've been super busy with my new job, there hasn't been but 3 days since I started in September that were less than 10 hours.  Weekends got eaten up by catching up on real life commitments and the odd 1/2 work day to catch up on late paperwork. Not helping things here, just prior (about 4 months) to me staring my new job I had my Jeep damn near totaled at work (a REALLY long story, but lets just say thereÂ’s a few reasons I DON'T work there anymore, and this was one of them) and that cut down on my spare time to get over and cast to just about zip. Most of the time I had no wheels from Castle Rock to Parker (my wife is in school full time getting her PHD, so late nights for her a lot), and even if I did have access to the other car I needed to get my Jeep back up and running ASAP which meant either running for parts or grabbing some wrench time.

HereÂ’s a good pick of an F-250 VS Jeep, F-250 1, Jeep 0

http://home.comcast.net/~ryan.comer/images/Jeep.jpg

Trust me, the damage was even worse than it looks as the firewall was buckled and the cowl and side were too.

AND YES, I did fix it all, and made a few "special modifications" myself.

  THE GOOD NEWS.  Steve is now able to be back 100% in his spare time, and my job is getting quickly caught up and ahead.  My personal real life obligations are getting caught up too (I used to have hobbies, now I have a HOUSE.) and with winter coming thankfully most things can fall by the wayside until spring now. And, the Jeeps back up and running.

  What that means for everyone owed a kit RIGHT NOW, is that I should be able to spend at least 1 full day a week pulling TIEs and other stuff.  For me, I've come along far enough that my Junior Padawan Resin Monkey status has been upgraded to Senior Padawan Resin Monkey, which mean faster pours and mold turns which means more parts and kits in a given day with a lot fewer mispours and unusable casts. I'm finding that for TIEs what it used to take a day for me to produce I can now get three times a much done in the same day. Trust me, thatÂ’s a LOT of fracking parts (and kits.).

Between Steve and I that means we should be fully caught back up on TIES as fast as we humanly can, as well as the other stuff thatÂ’s out there DONE.  Know that we've both spent as much time as possible getting things done to get everyone taken care of up until now, and the amount of time we'll both have from now on is going to only go up from here barring some catastrophe we can't foresee right now. 

  I want to thank everyone for their patience, trust me when I say that I had NO idea what I was in store for when I volunteered to help get Steve caught up on kits from pre-deployment.  A lot goes into a TIE, and even more in some of the other stuff we've been working on. We got that knocked out fairly fast for the most part, and now we'll work on getting the rest out too.  It will get done, just hang in there a bit longer. I'm looking forward to hearing kit reviews as they go out, and being able to FINALLY give those of you on the waiting list a shout and being able to tell everyone "as soon as you send the $, you're in the box kit will be on its way."

  Ryan

"This is MY Force power, its called a BLASTER."

For those of you with concerns over Steve's ability to deliver, please bear with me for a  few moments.

I had a chance to visit Steve this past Saturday. Let me tell ALL of you what an amazing job this guy is doing. Trying to juggle his military and health issues, I'd say he is doing an INCREDIBLE job trying to keep up with you guys. He really is concerned on getting kits out, but you must all understand, he is TRULY a "Garage Kit" manufacturer. Everything he cranks out is done right there in his garage, with top notch equipment and supplies. He doesn't skimp on anything to get you the right product.

He let me observe and learn how he makes mold boxes, pours the rubber, and pressure casts parts. He is meticulous and very detailed. He makes sure what he puts together is as close to perfect as possible.

Folks, it may take some time to get what you ordered, and I understand your frustrations (been there), but believe me, Steve is working his tail off, and I think you'll find whatever your wait, you WILL get it, and you WILL love it..

Keep supporting him, be patient and understand, he's doing this stuff for us.

Thanks for listening to my soapbox.

-Sean

Post #186  (forum post #40703)
Author    : belleauwood
Date      : Dec 17, 2005 at 9:26 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hey gang,

  I just wanted to drop a line to everyone and let them know that today was a VERY good casting day.  For those of you waiting on standard TIE's, Steve and I got a bunch done. Casting was slightly slowed by the somewhat cold temp in the garage as the resin was nice and pre-chilled thanks to the lovely cold weather here and took a bit longer to kick, and us resin monkeys are TROPICAL critters. That cold means a break between pours to warm up by the Kerosene heater and get the feeling back in the digits, garage + winter in CO + falling snow = COLD resin monkey. For those waiting on other kits, a lot of work was done on that too.  A good solid  11.5 hour day of casting, molding and mastering. 

    Its always amazing to look at the end of the day and see the "make", and I'm looking forward to seeing some "I got mine" posts as soon as these get in the mail and cycle through the busy USPS system. Y'all damn well better post (with PICS.) when ya get yours, as we're busting our hump to get these to you, and thats what keeps me going on cold days like this.

Next weekend Steve and I are taking off due to Christmas, and the following we both hope to knock out some more before the New Year, hopefully both days to make up for the Christmas break.  In between, I know Steves planning on working some more tomorrow and Monday, as well as what he can get done in the evenings after work, and I'm hoping to get a few evenings in if I can too. They're coming, as promised, just keep hanging in there.

  Ryan

"This is MY Force power, its called a BLASTER."

Anyone attempted to cut out the resin koolshade infill and replace it with the real stuff?  I have got the koolshade ready to go but before i start cutting out the resin, i would like to know if anyone had any pitfalls or problems trying this?

Post #200  (forum post #75742)
Author    : cobywan
Date      : Mar 7, 2006 at 10:13 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I would advise against it.  The wings get thicker as you move to the central hub.  Two flat cast halves would have made that problem go away.  You might want to get the hero wings or use what  was cast.  Otherwise you will need to make wedge shaped bacings for your Coolshade.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #201  (forum post #75751)
Author    : Aegis159
Date      : Mar 7, 2006 at 10:31 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Or he could first make a template of each section of the wing in sheet styrene. Then attach the coolshade to the templates and glue them in place on the wing.

Post #202  (forum post #86265)
Author    : swpropmaker
Date      : Mar 29, 2006 at 8:27 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hey guys,

I have just finished the Hero Wing star mold (long time on this one.)  This means I pressure cast just the Wing Stars NO resin Screen and NO Bubbles.  You need four to do a Hero Koolshade build up. 

I would advise not to try to cut the resin screen out of a standard TIE wing.  The process is almost impossible to get straight.  I will be able to do the HEROs again once i'm caught up with folks already waiting.  Shoot me a PM if you want to know more about the Hero wing Stars.

Also contacted my Distributor for Koolshade  to do One TIE fighter will require one 60" wide and 20" tall piece of material (exact no room for error.)  Cost including shipping is roughly $250 per TIE fighter for Koolshade alone.  That is bottom line no mark up whatso ever.  IF your thinking of doing a real screen version let me know and I'll see if we can get a cost break if we order a bunch.  I have 5 orders to put in and have previously ordered 5 sets.  So if your in need of the Koolshade they promised me 4 to 5 day Air mail once the orders have processed.   I can now have it drop shipped to your address.  They said shipping will be based upon actual address the quote here is for Denver Colorado, will be shipping from the UK.

Thanks for hangin in there, those that have been waiting.  Isle, need your address again please.

If there is any interest in the new Standard TIE kit and new Hero kits please PM.  

*No new orders will be taken till all backordered customers are shipped, but I will put you on an interested list and email when the kit is ready for shipping.*

Thanks guys.

Steve

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #207  (forum post #87269)
Author    : cobywan
Date      : Mar 30, 2006 at 7:31 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

It's the only way to replicate the "flash" effect of the pannels as you move around the model.  I think you could easily fake it with Evergreen slat styrene sheet and some strips.  But it won't be perfect.

I think the hero wings will look better than the solid ones that came with the standard kit.  The way the molds ballooned out in casting really detracts from the carefull detailing done on them.  The radial spars aren't straight and have a shallow "S" curve to them in profile.  It's the only problem I have with the kit.  I think flat casting the wings in two halves, or just the frames with room for my styrene idea would do the trick.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Date      : May 8, 2006 at 8:25 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hi Everyone,

Just resurrecting this thread as a very nice event happened this weekend.

I am in the same military unit as Steve (SWPropmaker).  This weekend, Steve was awarded the USAF Commendation Medal with Valor for exemplary service in Iraq.  I'm not going to go into much detail about his actions, other than they were heroic and he was in a intense gunfight with insurgents, Steve called in additional fire support, and saved the lives of many soldiers. 

The reason I'm posting this is to hopefully get those of you that have worried you won't get a TIE or any other model from Steve, understand that he is an Honarable, dedicated man, but soldier first. Steve will and ALWAYS delivers, just be patient. There are so many things going on for those of us in the military. Many things can't be discussed. So when you see/hear a slight delay, think about the person(s) who are doing this, for you.

Anyways, just wanted to let you all know about this incredible accomplishment for Steve, and join me in congratulating him on this most honorable award.

-Sean

CessnaDriver (and all of you),

Thank you.... That tribute was and is incredibly emotional for me, and I'm sure those that serve. I won't lie and say that didn't give me both goosebumps, and some tears.  So many folks that are not in the military will never understand what/who we are.  That tribute is simply amazing, with little words, and great photos, it spoke to me very deeply.  There is no way to express to you the emotion something like that does for someone like me.  Thank you for that link, it's nice to see the appreciation and support.

If I may for a moment... Years back, during the Gulf War, I remember leaving my base and protesters were yelling and throwing things at us as we left the gates. It was terrible, and I'll never forget that.

TODAY, all Americans, whether I'm in a store, in my car, or anywhere in public in uniform, I constantly get handshakes, thanks and appreciation for serving. It is nice to see the country take a different view towards us.

Anyways, I didn't mean to take this modeling topic off-topic, but appreciate everyone jumping in, understanding my buddy Steve, and supporting us all.

-Sean

I think that anyone who riles against steve just needs o chill. Don't buy kits from him. It's that simple. He is not in business as a retailer to provide "7 day service" or "just in time" delivery of inventory. I know of no one who has ever not received their kit...including me. I have waited almost two years for the "unspoken project" to arrive. If I had the ambition or smarts  to make these kits; to design these kits I would, I don't, and obviously most of us here don't either. So.....if you order a kit please be patient.....sometimes it requires uber patience......and uber-uber patience......otherwise, quit whining or don't order. Jeez....sorry guys, in the grand scheme of things this just isn't important. Steve has a job, a career, a FAMILY......has been deployed to Iraq, and lives in Colorado.....(inside joke). I know guys who freaked out when he was deployed because there was a delay. Come on.....grow up..

Post #346  (forum post #500310)
Author    : swpropmaker
Date      : Jan 27, 2008 at 10:07 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

Hey guys here’s an update.  I was about to put the interceptor wing under rubber but thank goodness I didn’t!  I knew that the light diffuser material was in the wrong scale to match perfectly and that always bothered me.  

This past week I was going through the Detention facility (Jail) in Laramie Wyoming (I am a cop in Cheyenne) and you wont believe what I found!  That’s right 1973 light diffuser material with the correct squares per inch!

What does this mean?  It means both the Vader and Interceptor project will have the correct material!   

Check out the pattern on the left… that’s the new stuff… the larger patter is incorrect.

I’ve already molded the screen material and today I am cutting the inserts. Thanks for being patient.  With this new discovery I’m sure this Interceptor will be the best release to date.

[IMAGE: https://www.therpf.com/forums/attachments/300942085-gif.883260/]

[IMAGE: https://www.therpf.com/forums/attachments/300942092-gif.883261/]

I have started the guns and wing end caps and hull parts.  For botht he TIE Fighter orders and Interceptors.  Both wings will be molded at the same time.

Steve

Post #369  (forum post #508678)
Author    : belleauwood
Date      : Feb 7, 2008 at 11:18 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

Guys,

 Just an FYI.  

  1st-  Steve is currently going to be VERY busy for the next few months.  He started his new career as a Police Officer and started the very intensive academy last week.  I'm guessing, with commute time, etc, that he's only going to have about a full day a week to both see his family AND pour molds and casts.

  2nd-  I can no longer get by and help Steve out like I used to, my career as a State Trooper has taken me about 2 1/2 hours away.  So I'm no longer able to be his full time resin monkey.  Though once I'm done with my field training in the end of this month and switch to the "normal" 5 on 4 off schedule I might be able to get by and help him out like I used to. We have talked about it and it could happen.

  3rd-  Steve WILL get his orders out, he is good for it and always has been.  In his own words, he sometimes may be slower than Christmas, but eventually, he does get there. I know its frustrating to wait,  I've been on BOTH sides of that coin.  Thats why Steve ate so big $$ on the BRSF and ATST, he fronted everything so that when he took $ for it, he could ship right away having product in hand.  Its VERY hard for a GK'er to do that, initial start on a kit is VERY pricey.

 4th- Those waiting on TIES- The wing mold failed after an odd curing resin pour *I* did more that 6-7 months ago locked and ruined it.  Its a biatch to remold, and takes a good sized slug of rubber to do. Its on the bench to redo from the last time I talked to Steve, he was retouching the master and getting it ready to remold. He was waiting for the INT to remold it because thats all going to come from the same $1K rubber kit.

  Those waiting on "Others" like the PD, he has plans to mold that soon too since he had "farmed" out the original hulls and the person doing that has been tied up with their "real world" job for a long time and looks to be for awhile, and he wants to get you ALL taken care of as promised.

  AFAIK, thats the only 2 types of kits owed right now, and WHY they are owed.  If you are owed anything else, LMK and I *Might* be able to tell you whats going on if I know.

 So, please be understanding of his current situation.  Its not easy going from career military at the top of the NCO totem pole and back down to a lowly recruit. Trust me, I went from where I was to the State Patrol Academy, and it doesn't matter WHAT you did before, they do a DAMN good job of "tearing you down" and getting you into the "mold".

   Factor in that he's in WY, his family is in CO still, and he's trying to sell the house AND go to a VERY intensive Academy and try on the weekends to catch up on homework and his family, AND pour molds and casts, and he's a VERY busy guy right now.  In fact, I don't think he gets online but maybe 1 day a week right now. I haven't even been able to catch him on the phone since he started his academy, and we normally talk at least 1-2 times a week.

 Hope this helps everyone and gets anyone worried a little less apprehensive.

  Ryan

Post #376  (forum post #508876)
Author    : moffeaton
Date      : Feb 8, 2008 at 9:09 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

Hey Dave,

With all due respect, you're fooling yourself if you think Ryan can get your model. Only Steve can. I have been in your shoes and it was a crappy journey to getting the model deal completed. Good luck.

You are going to REALLY need it. 

And if you think Steve is the best, you need to do your homework. There are MUCH nicer kits out there. Just not in the same subjects he happens to sell. When you're the only game in town, of course you are considered the best, you know?

There is no excuse for the delays I experienced and sub-par castings I received (and therefore at the time judged Steve by) for him to consider himself a "business". His current back log does not concern me, but does that mean I cannot tell someone what happened to me? It is on topic, right? As a kit maker, if you want to elevate yourself past hobbyist and into the realm of "master model caster", you have to provide quality and timely deliveries. That is all I am saying.

Every time you guys chime in with talk of "he will eventually deliver - be cool" you essentially give him a free pass to NOT deliver. You guys are selling yourselves short - do you not see that?!

And I have seen the ESB and ROTJ walker kits in the flesh - the castings are a LOT nicer than what was expected 10 years ago, but guys, this is 2008. You can get flawless castings with a little forethought and effort. Steve isn't even casting these - he has said that he has his kid doing the pouring for him - do you know what you are paying for?

I am just tired of people giving casters a free pass on foggy delivery dates, over-extended work loads, and dodgy parts, when there is a standard - a very attainable standard - that can be met. Steve has no love for me and I got nothing to lose since I have no outstanding orders, so why not say what other people are too afraid to say. I've got the balls to do it - don't get all irritated with me for saying what others say privately, okay?

Thank you.

I'm buying from very talented hobbyists, artists, really full blown professional level ablilities far beyond my feeble hands. I know they have real jobs. So I hear what your saying, but I also know I am not ordering from Master Replicas exactly, which of course had huge delays for many items over the years as well. And that is a full on major business entity. 

But your point is a good one, it's real money we put down. 

Pulling a "Scotty" is more preferred I think,

Maybe you think you can get it done in an early window, better to give a much larger window just in case.

I remember some advice when I was doing my own musclecar project. 

Calculate all costs and time needed. And then double it. 

I recently ordered a prop, put down a half payment, and not too long later the builder realized he was selling them far too cheap for his time and efforts, and had to raise prices dramatically. I got in under the wire, and he will honor the original price.

But clearly even years of experience was not enough for him to realize the actual time needed and appropriate costs. 

Even NASA has these problems.

Post #384  (forum post #510283)
Author    : swpropmaker
Date      : Feb 10, 2008 at 1:50 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

Wow,  

Looks like I’ve missed some stuff this week.  Thanks Jason for the heads up, its always refreshing to know we have folks out there ready to comment on how to do a better job. I do appreciate your comments; they have in the past made a difference on how I do business.  Thanks a million.

By the way my Son poured the majority of the ESB and ROTJ ATST’s  over 100 Satisfied customers many have stated it was the BEST castings they have ever seen.

Also who I farm out projects to is my business.  Many of the dealings are through trades so the caster can get a free casting of things.  Matter of fact there was only two projects farmed out ever and that was only a portion of the kit.  Helped a few resin brothers out.  Thanks Mike S.!

Hey Ryan, thanks for the cover man!  This Police academy is a mutha!  I’ve been staring at the Criminal law stuff for so long my eye’s are bleeding!! Maybe you can grab the resin bottles again when your done with the FTO program..you know its always open to you.

Anyhow back to business at hand…

Guys here is an update on the TIE and Interceptor.   The wing is under one side of rubber.  Because the jackets are already done I will take the molds to Wyoming this week with my vacuum chamber and pour the back side.  Then we will be in full production.  The Tie Wing Masters are tip top and ready for clay.  I pull the rubber of the hero masters (we found the last part so its 100% complete accurate! (Thanks Dan!)   I will try to get at least the FG jackets done tonight so I can pour them with the interceptor.  Here are some pics of the first set of 10 of 20 parts..each kit will have a sitting and standing pilot included.

Check the pics out for quality. There will be no problems.

[IMAGE: https://www.therpf.com/forums/attachments/303407547-gif.883347/]

[IMAGE: https://www.therpf.com/forums/attachments/303407580-gif.883348/]

[IMAGE: https://www.therpf.com/forums/attachments/303407570-gif.883349/]

[IMAGE: https://www.therpf.com/forums/attachments/303407559-gif.883350/]

I will be running the TIE’s with the Interceptors.  I expect to start having the sets together in about two weeks.  Detail sets are done, Hulls are being done this week and the wings are following.  This is the most accurate version yet.  So those that have waited (who I’ve made contact with) don’t think any more versions will be done, this is as close as you can get.

I know waiting is frustrating.  I’ve offered refunds o those that waited but have been told they would rather have the kit.  It’s the best one yet both versions!  I ordered 10 sets of KOOLSHADE  and will be having them dropped shipped to the hero folks.  Once the molds are squared away I will get ahead like I did with the AT-ST’s and folks will be able to get them shipped out a day after payment is made.

I tried doing a mass email thing but it doesn’t look like it went through.  I will update here on Sundays with pictures.  If you want to contact me with question DON’T POST IT IN THE THREAD!  I don’t read the RPF Monday through Friday.  Shoot me an email sneisen@comcast.net and I will go the Library on Thursday’s so I can check my mail the police department has blocked ALL in and outbound web mail.     

Please find a bit more patience and all your TIE dreams will come true!   Promise.

Steve

Check the pics out for quality. There will be no problems.

[IMAGE: https://www.therpf.com/forums/attachments/303407547-gif.883351/]

[IMAGE: https://www.therpf.com/forums/attachments/303407580-gif.883352/]

[IMAGE: https://www.therpf.com/forums/attachments/303407570-gif.883353/]

[IMAGE: https://www.therpf.com/forums/attachments/303407559-gif.883354/]

I will be running the TIE’s with the Interceptors.  I expect to start having the sets together in about two weeks.  Detail sets are done, Hulls are being done this week and the wings are following.  This is the most accurate version yet.  So those that have waited (who I’ve made contact with) don’t think any more versions will be done, this is as close as you can get.

I know waiting is frustrating.  I’ve offered refunds o those that waited but have been told they would rather have the kit.  It’s the best one yet both versions!  I ordered 10 sets of KOOLSHADE  and will be having them dropped shipped to the hero folks.  Once the molds are squared away I will get ahead like I did with the AT-ST’s and folks will be able to get them shipped out a day after payment is made.

I tried doing a mass email thing but it doesn’t look like it went through.  I will update here on Sundays with pictures.  If you want to contact me with question DON’T POST IT IN THE THREAD!  I don’t read the RPF Monday through Friday.  Shoot me an email sneisen@comcast.net and I will go the Library on Thursday’s so I can check my mail the police department has blocked ALL in and outbound web mail.     

Please find a bit more patience and all your TIE dreams will come true!   Promise.

Steve

I am busting my hump to get everything out so please bear with me if I'm not on the board as im in the garage!  Shoot me a email to make sure i hear from you sneisen@comcast.net

Steve

I have a order of things here so as they are done they will ship.  Pelase hang in there a bit longer and know I am working as hard and fast as i can!  Hope all is well with yo all..

Steve

First, he has only shipped three kits, one for each of the pattern builders and the third to Bob for his build up for Kurt, which is being used for publicity.    Steve is not taking any new orders until he has finished shipping kits to those individuals who preordered and have already paid.  Those preordered and paid kits will be shipped in the order in which payment was received; and Steve is hoping to get those finished this weekend.  Steve will try to reach those persons that have preordered and paid this Friday evening or Saturday Morning.  If you have preordered and feel you must speak to him you can call his mobile phone at 303-817-9339, he is in the “Mountain Time” zone.  Thanks  Dan  P.S.  Happy  Easter

I just start building and make it up as I go, there's really not much more you can do. Get out a piece of paper, go and get about 10 different colors you think are right, start mixing them in different combinations, then pick the one that looks the closest to you.

Post #500  (forum post #546490)
Author    : CessnaDriver
Date      : Mar 31, 2008 at 10:16 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

Guy Cowen said:

			Got my Tie Int today, all good apart from a few little worries, there is def not enough T track to go around the wings & my wings are quite banana shaped. What is the best way to straighten them out? How many pieces of T has everybody received, I got 6 but to do one wing would be at least 4?
		

Click to expand...

 

I found on my salzo X-wing, that soaking the fuselages in hot water and putting weights on them over night straightened them up fine. 

They were a little bowed. I used this technique to also get the end cap to fit properly, it was a little large so I again, soaked the fuselage in hot water and bent the end ever so slightly so things would line up properly.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

Hey guys,

Gone for a few weeks, looks like the natives are getting restless, understandably so.  Im pretty sure I had my cell phone number put up here so folks could contact me if they had questions as I would not be on line for a few weeks during the move.  So here is the first official update from new shop Cheyenne.  (I’ll post pictures tomorrow now that my connection is up)   

HERO TIE FIGHTER  the new hero mold for the wing has be remolded, with the final detail part on the hub has been found!  The wing is now 100% accurate and complete.  I will be running these as soon as the shop is up (will post pics )   

STANDARD TIE FIGHTER  The standard wing mold that was made when I poured the Interceptor molds and was damaged during the move.  The moving company packed the detail side of the RTV mold against the outer shell of the fiberglass mother mold, both wing molds were cut and details sheared away.  (I will post pics of the damage)  I will be getting a insurance claim on this, they also destroyed my 50” plasma TV.  

*** I did find a hole cutting drill bit that completely cores out the center Hull ball.  Its has more  room for a cockpit than ever.  Plus I’m throwing in a sitting TIE pilot to boot! The master pattern is ready so all I have to do is clay it up in the existing shells and pour the RTV.  Its on the first to do list in the new digs. 

TIE INTERCEPTOR  Those that are waiting for the INTERCEPTOR it survived the move and the hulls and detail parts are and have been completed. I will run the wings when the shop is up and running in a week or so.  I’ve been getting lots of requests for this kit but will not ship them until those that have pre ordered receive theirs.  This goes for the Standard TIE as well.  

Those that cant wait any longer for the Hero/Standard TIE’s kits please email me and I will issue a full refund.  If you want the kit please be patient and I will deliver. I will keep you updated as much as possible with production   If you cant wait and HAVE PAID please shoot be a email and I’ll get a refund to you.. If I do not hear from you I will assume you want the kit and keep pressing forward.  Please email me at sneisen@bresnan.net

Since I am a one man show I have many projects going at once, sometimes it gets overwhelming.  My phone number has never changed, I never run and hide, just sometimes I get busy with work family and other things.   Call me if you want to discuss your order, timelines, what’s going on as you will indeed get an answer. Heck if you just wanna chat, gimme a call.  Typing it here with emotion cons and “where’s my kit” will go answered until I log on again which could be up to a week.  I want all your questions answered and don’t want you to wait.  My connection is up now so I hope to be on more often.  If any of you have moved I hope you understand the stress and time constraints it puts on you and the entire family.  Please hang in these and things will get back to hopping soon.  I have 3 weeks left in a 15 week police academy and will soon start field training (13 weeks)  at least it will be a 4 and 3 schedule so I will have a whole day dedicated to making kits!

Thanks guys

Steve

I just read through the thread and will try to answer each of you individualy via pm or email.  I will say this THOSE OF YOU that want to come here and flame for the sake of being an jerk, go somewhere else.  We dont need your snyde comments, especialy when you have absolutley nothing to do with any of it. After reading through these threads I'm not sure now if I missed anything during my offline time. Ive shipped and delivered hundreds of kits during my time here and unfortunalty there have been several that have waited too long in the process.  I have always shipped some way later than others but shipped non the less.  Like some have done, if you cant wait scracth build it.  Making kits as a hobby is a huge stressor.  Anyone that has done it knows what I'm talking about if you never have you really cant say anything cause you really  dont know the time required to pull it off.  I have to laugh reading people's posts that have never talked to me or have anything to do with the TIE Fighter post making comments..  does it make you feel good to get the pitch forks out and burn torches and get the crowd  riled into a fevered pitch?  Makes no sense to me.. no sense at all.  I make models in my spare time and make kits as well so other fans can have a little piece of film history in their collections.. thats all.  By no means is any part time kit maker makinhg a fortune at this.  Material prices are sky rocketing, equipment costs are out of this world and the individual time required to do this is un heard of for a hobby.   

I just got finished talking with a fellow kit producer/scratch builder and we both agree man sometimes its not worth it.  So once I'm caught up on TIEs and Interceptors things will be slowed down a great deal.  I thought getting rare kits to the fans like me would be cool but not being able to keep up with all the requests for info, orders ect is most likley a bit much for what I want out of this hobby. The negative folks here that post just to cause trouble cheapens this place. 

My TIE fighter is detail to detail accurate to the ILM filming minature.  Both versions.  10 years hunting the parts lots of great people pitching in, I thank them all.  Did you guys know i dont even own one.  Matter of fact i dont have anything that I make in my collection.  I'm so busy when I make stuff it goes out the door.  There have been a handful of dissatisfied customers who like to post often. However there are a whole lot more happy ones (you just dont hear from them)  I try to do the right thing that is why 'm offering the refunds.  Wait no longer cause I'm done listening to those who have nothing to do with this take cheap shots at me and my craft.     I'm extreamly slow in some situations, years slow on some (im reminded of this all the time) Ive offered refunds but folks say they would rather have the kit.  With that comes the wait.  I wish it didnt happen but things happen and I'm sorry.  I have never ran with anyones hard earned money.  It usually gets dumped right back into the next project.

This thread is for TIE Fighters and Interceptors   Thats what I do.  Im on it guys, working on the shop once its organized I'll be inproduction.  New Hero and Standard TIE master molds!  Clean bubble free castings, TIE fighters as far as the eyes can see, maybe this time I'll keep one for myself!

Steve

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

Guys,

Thanks a million.  I'm glad you are so excited about the new TIEs!  The wings have never looked better.  I use to have to mold the Hero stars by hand no pressure chasing all the bubbles with a stylus but now after the move I got an idea.  I purcheced a heavy duty dolly and strap it to my 60 gallon pressure chamber.  I then set it down for its horizontal feed. I then made a shelf that molds can sit level on.  This way i can put molds that are one sided in and pressureize them.  Will take pics of the first castings as soon as the new resin arrives.  Any one expierence trouble with resin moving from different climates?  I have about a half a kit left it when it cures it foams out of control and seeps like crazy, called Poly Tek  they had no answer (possibly) water contamination.  Not sure so I ordered another 10 gallons to see whats what.

Will uploadpics of the in progress shot later today.  man its great to have internet up and running again!

Steve

Post #594  (forum post #604282)
Author    : moffeaton

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

And I'd just like to add this:

If you owe someone something, and you have internet access now, how freaking hard is it to post on an internet forum? I read this thread and come away with a feeling that there is a distinct lack or respect for the people waiting for their kits, waiting for responses about kits, and in less-publicized but more-troubling situations, the lack of follow-through with compensation for the pattern makers themselves!

The way I see it, Steve is a casting service with a great talent for selling the sizzle/concept. Meanwhile, there's pattern makers and plenty of customers and potential customers falling through the cracks. And no one can even get a real picture of how big the situation is, because half of the "waiting list" is too intimidated to speak up, lest they get an earful from the tempermental fella holding all of the cards. 

And yes, in the interest of full disclosure, I have been on the receiving end, and had to make an awfully big stink to get my TIE fighter. It ended in bad blood. It'll happen again to some other unlucky person here. Of course, I've received the full-on anger from Steve, so I have nothing to lose by posting all of this. So here's a call to arms for the people with more to lose than I do, and who are thinking the same things I am.

Break the cycle, someone! PLEASE. It'd be easiest for Steve to do it with a simple posted update. You know?

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

Found it,  called Steve and got him on the first try!!!  
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
    He was literally en-route to his resin supplier to pick up 4 gallons of the stuff.    He told me that his moulding/pouring table is now cleared and he's gonna begin pouring up the Hero TIE kits tomorrow morning if not sooner.  He is doing those first as they are the oldest outstanding orders.  He said all the owed hero kits will go out beginning this Wednesday since he is finally back into the swing of things in his workshop.    Once the Hero TIE's are out he will begin filling the TIE Standard backorders.  The new pressure chamber he's using is turning out fantastic castings that will blow our minds from his descriptions.  I believe the occasional bubble riddled castings are a thing of the past.   I can believe this as I use a pressure pot myself when casting small items.   
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
  Once the TIE standards are finished and away,  he'll begin the Interceptors in earnest.  Again,  everything is in place for the Interceptors,   but they are the most recent orders,  so will be in limbo until the hero/standard TIE orders are fulfilled.    Steve also says he's gonna update on this thread as these backorders are sent out so folks know where their orders stand,  rather than everyone wondering where their order stands.  

Steve says he'll update this thread in person tonight or tomorrow and re-iterate or correct what I've just posted here.  He may even have "Hero" first casting photos as a nice bonus.   
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Steve if I've forgotten anything you'll have to forgive me,  I've been on vacation for 10 days and am still on "Island time".   

This is the first time I've had the priveledge of chatting with Steve and it was a nice and informative discussion.  If anyone is hesitant to call him,  don't be.  He's a genuinely nice fella and doesn't avoid his callers.    I've heard all too well,  the hectic schedule of police training  and have a bit of a soft spot for those men and women pursuing such a career.    More than a few of my patients are in law enforcement and have told me their rigorous schedules and demands during the training phase of their career.   My hat is off to you guys.  

Anyway,  I hope my update is an encouragement and with any luck,  I'll be able to post photos of a brand spankin new Hero TIE kit in the next week or so.  

I'd like to thank Moffeaton for reminding me that I could just pick up the phone and call Steve.  It was wise advise.  I'm quite glad I did so.   
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

peace guys,

Post #645  (forum post #622577)
Author    : vaderdarth
Date      : Jul 8, 2008 at 6:59 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

I think he's trying to move in the direction of no new orders until his old orders are fulfilled.   I know he's working out a way to not take funds from customers until their package is ready to box up and ship out.......at least.......for future new projects.   He gets tons of email daily,  so be patient,  he'll answer your emails David.  

Moffeaton,  yes his castings are a huge improvement to quote Steve.    He said all the detail pieces he has collected now get Pressure moulded and cast prior to building up the protos.  Then the normal sized pieces can then be pressue moulded and cast as well.  The only things he can't pressure cast are the oversized parts like the TIE wings etc....   Those are still having to be cast flat where he can put alot of weight on top of the mould so that each wing comes out nice and uniform.  But as you can see...........the new moulds/resins he's using produce nice flat cast pieces.  You'll still see a bubble here and there,  but nothing like the older techniques.   I noticed the same thing with Randy Cooper's offerings.  With time,  his castings have gotten cleaner and cleaner.  Luckily,  we get to be the recipients of these improvements.  

We do  have to keep this in mind............when a studio makes a mould and casts from that mould...........their intent is usually to pull 1-5 castings max out of a given mould.   The moulds that have such fine and intricate detail just don't last long as the parts tear them upon demoulding.    So when we talk about producing these pieces in a bit higher quantites.........moulds frequently have to be remade and repaired.  The castings, in turn start to show more signs of problems as the mould gets more and more used.   Hence the re-moulding etc...   Not all castings are perfect as we all know.  But at least folks like Steve and Randy will send you a replacement piece should one be "outside the norm".    I've been a customer of both of these guys for a long while and that has always been their way of doing business.  
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Dave

Post #707  (forum post #633593)
Author    : imaginager
Date      : Jul 23, 2008 at 8:31 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

DARKSIDE72 said:

			Alan, 

You're awesome bro! 

J 

Any info you can pass along as to the wing construction would be great. Template wise etc..
		

Click to expand...

 

No prob. Let's see...I never did make any templates. In fact, long story short, I cut each piece of styrene sheet for the wings custom for the wingstars I'd paired up for each side. ILM has a grand tradition of asymmetry, and I saw no reason to deviate. Congrats on your kit, btw. I had to remove about half the height on each spar/spoke on each wingstar in my kit to get the correct appearance on the wings. I tried to keep a consistent height of 3.0 mm. Looks like the newer kits are good to go out of the box. Cool. 

Anyway, you need to select which version of the TIE you want to do, ANH or ESB, because it affects the wing construction. The H-channel on the ESB's rests on the tips of the stars. However, on ANH the wingstar spars/spokes extend all the way out to the outer edge of the H-channel. That variable governs the dims of the styrene sheet. Also, don't forget that the styrene is inserted inside the H-channel, so you need to carefully measure the depth of the channel to get the right dims. I'll say it right now: I screwed up my first set of styrene inner wings. LOL

Once you have all of those components sized and cut, test fit and are happy, then you can use paper to trace each of the 24 templates to cut the Koolshade. This may seem like a lot of unnecessary work, but if you blow it with the Koolshade, you're done: there's only enough material to do 2 wings. Now, when you lay out the templates on the Koolshade, you also need to make sure that the pattern is running consistent - that is, parallel to the outer edge of the wing. I photographed a real TIE to attempt to determine if the shades are up or down, relative to the wing's edge. I forget which way it goes.

[IMAGE: kshade.jpg]

[IMAGE: kshade1.jpg]

Test fit. Test fit. Test fit. And then, test fit some more. I used 5 minute epoxy on mine, and after about a year, I had 2 spars/spokes lift off the Koolshade - they wanted to return to their cast position. So, on the advice of REL I injected some CA and it bonded quite nicely. Epoxy is tough because it wants to "squish" and ooze out from under the spokes if applied with a heavy hand. Less is more. If I had it to do again, I'd try CA first. Oh, make sure you paint your styrene sheets before you fix the Koolshade to the styrene. 

That's about all I can think of off the top of my head. I used rare earth magnets to attach the wings to the pylons. Never had any trouble with them and mine has been on display since December 2006!

Sounds like Steve has made some improvements, so I will be anxiously waiting to see more Hero buildups. I gotta tell ya, I cringe looking at the pics of mine, now. This wasn't originally intended to be a kit. Gotta give props to Steve for taking it on and refining it over the years. It was a hell of a job! I wouldn't have had 2 sticks to rub together, otherwise. That said, I'd love to scratch a one-off someday. I have many of the donor kits. But, I have so many SW subjects to finish it will probably never happen. The Nice-N Hero is an impressive finished model.

Good luck Jamie, and everyone else! Let's see some buildup threads...

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

Jamie,

glad you liked what you got.  There is a suttle difference in the wing edging between the ANH version and ESB version.  The best way to descibe it is look at an side view of a ANH wing... the top of the H beam (that trims the wing edge) ends at the end of the wing star. 

On the ESB version the bottom of the H beam (that trims out the wing) starts and the end of the wing star (need u channel to complete to help hide the seem)  

So the ESB wing is larger than the ANH wing by the heigth of the H beam.

Steve

That material is undercut all over the place by its very nature, so you'll have to fill in the slats partially using clay. It could be tricky to mold. . .

The vertical "stripes" are really more like twisted ropes made of two pieces of thin wire. The slats are bronze metal strips woven into that wire.

Click to expand...

I have 8 square feet, but I don't know if that is enough. If they have black PVC, then you can get that if you like, but you're going to paint the whole model anyway. It shouldn't be too much trouble to paint the foam. Jamie says that 1/8" (0.125") is the right size to get, and I trust that he is correct. I haven't yet checked myself. There has to be enough width inside the 1/4" H column to accommodate the thickness of the foam and 2 layers (1 each side) of koolshade.

Oh, and I am fairly certain that the underside (the foam) gets painted black and the koolshade gets left as-is (since it is already black). It has a sheen to it, but it's not super-high gloss. I would bet that if you painted it with a gloss black, it might look too shiny.

If you can afford it, get some extra and play around until it looks right.

Post #746  (forum post #650114)
Author    : star-art
Date      : Aug 14, 2008 at 7:13 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

Foamcore? I would strongly recommend that you don't use that. First, on the ANH TIE, the only material in between the inner and outer layers of KoolShade was black paper. (That's right -- just thin black paper!) It was used only to prevent you from seeing right through the material. There was no underlying panel in there -- at least not on the damaged TIE recently sold at auction.

Second, foamcore warps very readily and so it is not dimensionally stable. The paper surface absorbs moisture which causes it to curl and thereby warp. In addition, the foam inside is not very dense and so it is pretty weak. This, combined with the paper layer on the outside, makes the material relatively fragile.

If you really need to use something like a foam composite sheet, a much better choice is Gatorboard (not Gatorfoam). Gatorboard isn't available in a 1/8-inch thickness (it starts at 3/16 inch), but it's tough as nails and is pretty much as dimensionally stable as quality plywood. It's hard has heck to cut and can dull your knife blade quickly, but it can be laser-cut beautifully. The outer paper surface of this material is impregnated with a tough resin.

Gatorboard is still susceptible to moisture, so it should be sealed. If you coat the surface with water-thin epoxy, you'll have a strong, lightweight, and dimensionally stable composite part that should be good for many years of service.

Why worry about this sort of thing? I don't hear it discussed very often, but models made out of a variety of materials can have problems like cracking, warping, and separating over time because different materials expand and contract at different rates. The safest situation is when the entire model is made of one material, like resin or fiberglass. When you have different materials combined together, it's wise to be careful. 

I've heard this from quite a few experienced experts, and it's the sort of thing museums take into account when acquiring models that are meant to be preserved for a lifetime. Just think of all the effort (and expense) that you are investing in your project. Do you want the finished result to stand the test of time?

If so, the key is keeping the model in a climate-controlled environment at all times. Avoid big temperature swings, direct sunlight, and, most of all, humidity. This is always a good idea when you build something out of non-homogeneous materials that can expand/contract at different rates -- especially wood or paper. Anything that is susceptible to moisture can actually swell if exposed to enough humidity.

Hope that helps! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

I don't claim to be any sort of expert on the TIE so I don't know for sure what was used on the wings for all the different models they made. I do know, however, that only paper was present on the vintage model that recently sold at Profiles. A friend of mine actually had his hands on that model so he got a real good look at it. 

To tell the truth, I can't imagine those wings staying flat with only the resin "arms" of the stars for structural support. That KoolShade is pretty heavy stuff. Back then they often secured it in place with hotmelt glue. So, you'd think something else would be needed for structural integrity.

When I finally get around to completing my own TIE, I'm thinking about using thin aluminum sheet in there as a "core."

Post #749  (forum post #650229)
Author    : GKvfx
Date      : Aug 14, 2008 at 11:52 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

Yeah, Charles, I think he was referring to what I call Sintra - http://store.foamboardsource.com/sintra-pvc-foam.html

I have some of the stuff and it is useful.  At 1/8" thicknesses, it's easier to cut that plex, lighter, and takes superglue really well (almost too well).  You can get thicker sheets as well.  It still warps when subjected to heat or water, but still good stuff.  It has a slightly pebbled surface on the top and bottom.  The sides, or any edges you cut, will have a cell texture as it is a dense foam.

As for the TIE, yep, I was amazed when I looked between the wing panels and saw paper sticking out.  It wasn't tracing paper mind you, but I was expecting the thicker piece of plastic.  Obviously, I didn't take it apart, but the wing seemed damned thin all the way to the hub.  And there was no trace of glue residue oozing out from between the koolshade slats.

Gene

Naw... build your own! More fun...

Is that Sintra stuff the same as this:

http://www3.towerhobbies.com/cgi-bin/wti0001p?&I=LXTLE0 ?

That's the stuff I had. It only comes in white and it's surface is harder than its interior. It's really nice stuff. I know that the Midwest sheets are not big enough for a TIE Wing, but I got some 0.040" 4' X 8' sheets from a local plastics supplier. The 0.040" is actually 1mm, and it comes in 2 and 3mm as well.

If the Sintra is the same stuff, I might look into that as well.

P.S. In the description for the Midwest foam it says "flexible." It is flexible, but thicker pieces take a lot to bend. It is rigid. If you held it out straight, it would not bend under its own weight. The 0.040" would, but not the thicker pieces. It does not scribe and snap well, but it's not hard to cut all the way through.

Post #761  (forum post #650812)
Author    : Flintlock
Date      : Aug 15, 2008 at 6:38 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

DARKSIDE72 said:

			The koolshade is right at .060 just put a mic on it. 

Yep there is a  difference between the styrene and ABS "H" beam. I didn't know this...  SO the abs has a .200" gap and the syrene has a .220" gap.  .80" material or  .140" me thinks .80"  woops!
		

Click to expand...

The Plastruct ABS H-Beam, if 1/4" is the correct size, has a 0.13" gap (0.25 - 2[0.060]), because the thickness of the wall is 0.060. If the Koolshade is indeed 0.060" thick, then this leaves only 0.010" in between them.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

			The Plastruct ABS H-Beam, if 1/4" is the correct size, has a 0.13" gap (0.25 - 2[0.060]), because the thickness of the wall is 0.060. If the Koolshade is indeed 0.060" thick, then this leaves only 0.010" in between them.
		

Click to expand...

Therein lies the problem. I do believe the correct H-beam is H-8 ABS, 1/4 in total width, 060 wall thickness. That leaves room for two layers of KoolShade and a very thin layer of paper in the gap. If you have 1/8 inch of KS + 1/8 inch of wing core material, it sounds like you're using a much larger H beam than the one on the original. :eek

Plastruct's large butyrate tubing stinks -- literally! I bought some almost 2 years ago for a project and had to put it out in the garage because of the strong odor. (It doesn't glue very well, either.) It still smells even today. Weird. . .

Yeah, plastic for structural support isn't often a good idea with large and/or heavy models. That's because plastic bends and warps and it gets brittle over time. A proper metal armature is the way to go. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

BTW, the cockpit canopy is actually supposed to be vacuformed. It's dome shaped, not angular. The frame is quite thin, too. Flintlock, try getting a sculpting tool for the scribing, you can achieve wider lines depending on the tool. You can also angle your tool to one side or the other as you make your scribes to achieve a wider scribe.

Post #789  (forum post #678300)
Author    : moffeaton
Date      : Sep 23, 2008 at 6:43 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

I use USPS online all the time -  a dozen packages a week sometimes. Never had one problem, especially like you describe. I love the online system too - saves time, especially when I send stuff to Japan (which is often!). I send model kits to Italy (which is notoriously flaky with packages), Germany, Spain, Canada, and Australia mostly. I require the buyer to pay for priority or EMS shipping. It's way more expensive, but it gets there within a week and is traceable. Man, you have had some bad luck with shipping-related hiccups - even in your new area post-move! I can maybe see it being a bad luck of the draw with a regional branch (there's a particular post office in Baltimore that I avoid like the plague - the staff are morons!)... but you're in a new area now, right? I hope you get better luck.

Do you get/provide tracking numbers? If not, do that from now on, with every single thing you send - that way, USPS is more accountable. Right now, it's "you said/they said" and it gets you nowhere when you need to prove shipment.

Ouch!  that sux Steve.  Sorry to hear that USPS is screwing around now.  This sort of crap I'd expect from UPS or Fedex,  but not USPS.   I'll tell you another thing with USPS,  their insurance is practically worthless too.   They make you provide your purchase receipts for whatever you are shipping if you ever want your money back.   If it's something hand made..........you're just out of luck as there is no way to provide a receipt for something you made.    That is a rip off.    Then assuming it all goes correctly,  it may be a year before your refund arrives.  There is absolutely no excuse for that.  

Dave
