Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

Hey everybody,

I have been working on filling all orders.  I currenlty have 3 ROTJ ATST (doing molds for new legs now), 10 TIE Interceptors, 7 TIE Fighters and 3 Y Wings complete.  (thats alot of work) 

Ive taken it upon myself to add upgraded parts to the interceptors and Tie fighter kits even though the original parts had already been made. Thats taking a kit longer than id like but they are far more accurate than the current ones.

Those of you waiting for a TIE kit that would rather just have the current Cockpit frame, canopy, hatch and rear section shoot me a email and i 'll send it with the parts the kit currently has.

Those that have waited I know its been a long ordeal...   the oly reason i need to take a new order is help with cost of resin and shipping.  Im not doing any runs..  just the one here and there to keep the kits going out.  

Below  are current kits in line for shipping.. off the top of my head..

TF and 2 y wings  rolando

TF and Interceptor Gort

ROTJ (new legs) Nils/Gonk27  (can send right away if you guys want the legs as they are.. to small  but cast and ready to go)

YWing Daytona

Tie wings Dean

GF replace damaged TW and hull details

remainding Interceptor orders...

and there are only a few others to take care of then i'm caught up.

There is one in transit.. TIE and Interceptor in post now to Eric.

I am working as fast as I can.. trust me...

I got in a hole and i'm digging out I can see daylight!  If you have questions about your order please call me or email 

I'll try to go through my PM box here and catch up..its like 33 pms.  The best way to get ahold of me is call me or email.  The kits are shipping.  I'll try to keep my pms answered.

I know it doesnt matter to most of you but we had a pretty serious family crisis the past couple weeks that required my full attention.  Through it all I continued to crank out owed kit, hence a basement full of parts.   I will continue to do so until everone is satisified.   On average i'm sending out 4 - 5 kits a week.

Thanks guys..  heres my info again.

sneisen@bresnan.net

(303) 817 9339  call collect if need be. 

Unfortunatly I DO NOT visit the forum much this past few months.  I'm trying to stay focused on running kits and not get distracted by so many great builds on this forum.  You can spend hours here admiring the work others are doing here!  

Steve

Post #871  (forum post #798244)
Author    : Zombie Killer
Date      : Feb 16, 2009 at 9:36 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

Darth_Nickel said:

			How did you get the new bottom hatch on. Mine looks like the bottom is molded into the hull. I am a moron at this stuff, so sorry if my question is dumb.
		

Click to expand...

I started out grinding it down using a 1 1/4" dia. drum sander in a hand drill to flatten it out untill there was just a little bit of the lip of the original cover left . Then i used a small drum sander on the dremel to eat some more untill it was super close, then used the same tool to eat a perimiter around the bottom about 1/8" in from the edge. Then a mini end mill on the dremel to clean it up and make a trench for the cover to go into.(see pic) Once i got it to fit i noticed the original top and bottom hatch was a little crooked so the new covers details didn't line up quite right with the hulls details. So i took a big file and squared up the top and bottom holes. The front and back were fine. Once i did this and recleaned out the bottom trench everything is pretty straight now. I can't wait to keep going on it but i'm close to having all my Hasbro Greivous ship mods done so i need to finish it first.

[IMAGE: DSC00073.jpg]

[IMAGE: DSC00075.jpg]

[IMAGE: DSC00076.jpg]

Post #884  (forum post #800408)

Date      : Feb 19, 2009 at 10:59 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

Nils said:

			Any idea on what to use?
		

Click to expand...

The originals had 5mm orange LEDS like in my pics but i am told the new orange LED's available are a whiteish color when unlit. You will have to use either red or the whitish orange ones, or try to source some of the old orange ones. I don't know where you can get them. Also made in the 70-80's are some orange LED's that look yellow when unlite. I just recently found some of them by accident looking for yellow ones in my parts bins. 

Hope this helps

I have been working on filling all orders. I currenlty have 3 ROTJ ATST (doing molds for new legs now), 10 TIE Interceptors, 7 TIE Fighters and 3 Y Wings complete. (thats alot of work)

Those of you waiting for a TIE kit that would rather just have the current Cockpit frame, canopy, hatch and rear section shoot me a email and i 'll send it with the parts the kit currently has.

Those that have waited I know its been a long ordeal... the oly reason i need to take a new order is help with cost of resin and shipping. Im not doing any runs.. just the one here and there to keep the kits going out. 

Below are current kits in line for shipping.. off the top of my head..

TF and 2 y wings rolando

TF and Interceptor Gort

ROTJ (new legs) Nils/Gonk27 (can send right away if you guys want the legs as they are.. to small but cast and ready to go)

YWing Daytona

Tie wings Dean

GF replace damaged TW and hull details

remainding Interceptor orders...

and there are only a few others to take care of then i'm caught up.

There is one in transit.. TIE and Interceptor in post now to Eric.

I am working as fast as I can.. trust me...

I got in a hole and i'm digging out I can see daylight! If you have questions about your order please call me or email 

I'll try to go through my PM box here and catch up..its like 33 pms. The best way to get ahold of me is call me or email. The kits are shipping. I'll try to keep my pms answered.

I know it doesnt matter to most of you but we had a pretty serious family crisis the past couple weeks that required my full attention. Through it all I continued to crank out owed kit, hence a basement full of parts. I will continue to do so until everone is satisified. On average i'm sending out 4 - 5 kits a week.

Thanks guys.. heres my info again.

sneisen@bresnan.net

(303) 817 9339 call collect if need be. 

Unfortunatly I DO NOT visit the forum much this past few months. I'm trying to stay focused on running kits and not get distracted by so many great builds on this forum. You can spend hours here admiring the work others are doing here! 

Steve

Guys,

Ok... uncle...    guys im working on it.  I ship every week.  I make kits every week.  

I am  plugging away as fast as one person can.  The only "NEW" orders are taken care of with a week to 10 days in some cases they have recieved thier items (non TIE/Interceptor) within 4 days but unfortunately those guys dont post.

Nick your kits are done (old hulls) was upgrading you to the new two part TIE hulls but I guess you cant wait any longer I'll ship what I have.  Email me if you would rather have the 2 parter with armeture.

Rolando.. The Y Wing head master is being 100% reworked upper and lowers with hollow centers.. as soon as that arrives your kits will ship.  The old version mold failed.  The Larger ATST legs are being molded now and will be ready.   

[IMAGE: 359161718.jpg]

All other TIE and Interceptor kit waiters I am shipping 3 to 5 kits a week.  I just took this picture of ready to box TIE and Interceptor kits  The reason these have not shipped is Im adding upgraded hatches, cockpit inserts, accurate pilots and canopys free of charge.  Couldnt see sending out the old version when I have the imporved more accurate parts finished. 

As far as someone else being the "king" of star wars kits... please  give them my email and  I will gladly negotiate the transfer of all my equipment, patterns and molds..  any takers? 

I would love to be a subject again in the studio scale kingdom.

I think the non kit producers here need to take several steps back and take a look at the big picture.  

 Me personally I haven't always seen eye to eye with Steve in the past. Hell I had to call him out at one point in time and was really pissed at him. 

That's water well under the bridge and I can say I'm glad we worked everything out and have a great working relationship. I'm proud to call him a friend.

Not only is he working damn hard to get his past orders out ASAP, new models are being developed for the future. I'm working on 4 of them myself. A group is divided working on many a subject, leaving Steve to work on his past commitments. Which he has been doing.  New information and detail has come to light and I know he's been adding that to his old Tie kits.

 He's a State Trooper, works evenings mostly and a married family man. YOU WILL get your kits! My point is that he's a human being too, you know? He will not rip any one off.  

If you're worried give him a call.  Even when he's on duty he will answer his phone.

 The quality of work being done is fantastic. His castings are gorgeous today and well worth any wait. Detail never before seen or had on studio models is being produced. ANH that is 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 I can guarantee that.  

Rolando, the Y cockpit is in my hands at the moment, give me a couple of weeks to finish up and return the master. It's a total overhaul of the model with a lot that needed fixing. John is working on the body. 

J

Click to expand...

 

There has never been a true SS kit of the ANH X-1 that I know of. It took the best donor part finders we know a long time to figure out what was used on it. Some fun finds on that one! :angel

The way this is working is once a kit it released it is soon retired to make way for new projects. No over-lapse, no waiting periods, and no getting behind. So every model will be a relatively small run. Retired for good? That remains to be seen. 

As far as the Red Y Martin, even though it wasn't ever seen on screen it does have a unique pedigree. So it's about a choice for the builder.

ralphee said:

			The Jammer wasnt used on screen, for a start i dont even think it was with ILM when shooting for the mini's was underway, it was sent, AFAIK to Elstree for the full size set mock ups...thats what ive heard anyhoo!

lee
		

Click to expand...

Lee, the Red Squadron Y-wing was built for Elstree reference and there are pics showing it there in company with Blue 1. It was incomplete - partial starboard engine only, no piping, etc. (The set mockup has the Red Squadron Y's paint scheme, easily picked by the grey nose panel on the port upper forwards surface.)

Both models were sent back to ILM; Blue Leader became Red 2 as is now well known and the Red Y was given a complete starboard engine and piping. We know this was done before the publicity shots in Famous Spaceships were taken, and there seems no reason to suppose the work wasn't done at the same time as the repaint of Red 2. I can't see why it wouldn't have been shot. But it's like finding Red 4 and Red 6 on screen...hard!

Still wondering what "Jammer" means BTW, there's no sign of EW gear on this ship, LOL!

Cheers,

Martyn

Re: STUDIO SCALE TIE FIGHTER   **UPDATED PICS**

Yes indeed for both:  1.   avoiding wing strut sag,  and  2. for having a mounting port built into the model framework.  The third reason would be because the originals were  built this way.  

Dave 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #1022  (forum post #879664)
Author    : Davy Jones
Date      : May 21, 2009 at 12:12 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Well the original armatures were a bit different. They seem to consist of two parts of metal tube and a machined metal rod that goes into it. That rod has mounting holes at each end in addition to the four mounting holes in the middle like we see on the replica. 

The way the rod stays in the tubes is there is a machined groove on the top of that rod and two allen bolts are tightened through the tubes and into that groove behind the pilot on either side.

Sort of a bizarre system but thats how they did it unless I am mistaken.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #1023  (forum post #880378)
Author    : vaderdarth
Date      : May 22, 2009 at 6:46 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

that description sounds like what Steve relayed to me about this armature.  It might not be identical,  but it should provide good support for the TIE body and wings and allow you to mount the bird to a panavise support.  

Dave 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Post #1049  (forum post #895251)
Author    : vaderdarth
Date      : Jun 6, 2009 at 7:04 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Steve,  I'm betting that it will do that until you can find a way to pour it all at once.  I'm betting that when you pour one side with the rod,  then flip it,  the second pour is curing unevenly from the heat of the first pour.............and unless that rod is 100% centered in the armature mould,  it will keep making the resin pull off to one side............and thus the warpage.  If at all possible,  pour the entire armature top to bottom in one go.  The risk of bubbles is not so  important on this part anyway.  
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
  Just a theory my friend.......

Dave

EUREKA! Ive increased the diameter of the internal rod to 1/4"  and it worked.. well till it started to cool then it warped.

[IMAGE: 367247427.jpg]

[IMAGE: 367247445.jpg]

[IMAGE: 367247445.jpg]

OK.. heres what Im going to do...  ive ordered a tube of ABS with an internal diameter of 1/4"  this will not expand and contract like the metal does... I will cast the ABS tube inside the armature then once cured straight I will epoxy a 1/4 steel rod inside for added strength.  Im thinking I will do this this time only and the next run will be metal armeture only....  once this is fixed I'll be shipping past due orders again with the new hulls and detail sets....

I'll post who getting what, when here....

Post #1064  (forum post #909235)
Author    : ILMwannabe
Date      : Jun 22, 2009 at 11:30 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Studio Scale TIE Fighter Colors

wooten said:

			I've been looking at various reference photos and since I'm new at this, I'm not sure about something.

Is the common one from ROTJ or something?  Some people also paint their TIEs more blue than grey.  I know (think) ESB and ROTJ props were kind of a bluish, but the ANH ones look more grey. What's right?
		

Click to expand...

That's a very controversial & hot topic & I'm sure that it's been discussed here before, but since we're both newbies I'll share what I've learned from reading the boards and various sources.

In the first film (A New Hope 1977) the TIEs don't look bluish at all, but in later films they did, this is why some folks build theirs gray. According to the book 'Famous Spaceships of Fact & Fantasy" published in 1978 the TIE's were painted a light gray blue, almost a powder blue (more gray than blue), but blue values are lost during film duplication and the bluescreen process. According to Lorne Petersen (ILM staff member) in his book "Scultping a Galaxy" the TIE's were painted in a Tamiya color which is no longer available ("Stormy Sea Blue") and barely passed bluescreen tests (you can't use blue on models with the bluescreen process because everything that is blue will become black like space).

Beyond that, it seems that some ships may have been painted a slightly bluer shade in later movies (it's hard to tell sometimes, it's a very tricky color) and yes there were differences between the various models, even amongst the "hero" and "pyro" versions. Some had longer laser cannons than others, some were missing the amber colored tips, different gray areas, darker window frames, slightly different wing panels, etc.

Hope this helps. I'll try to find a thread where this was discussed earlier . . .

I have an older Niesen TIE with the solid wings & I'm very happy with it. I plan to make my own armature for it & maybe hollow it out a little to make it lighter (it's pretty heavy!).

wooten said:

			I can't wait to get this kit.

I've been looking at various reference photos and since I'm new at this, I'm not sure about something.

In many buildups, if not all, people typically use this paint scheme:

[IMAGE: jv_tie_1.jpg]

[IMAGE: jv_tie_5.jpg]

Yet an original prop from ANH looks like this:

[IMAGE: profiles-in-history-tie-fighter-model-x425.jpg]

[IMAGE: eBay_Star_Wars_TIE_Fighter_2.jpg]

In particular, the second image of both is what concerns me..

Are both 'correct'?  Is the common one from ROTJ or something?  Some people also paint their TIEs more blue than grey.  I know (think) ESB and ROTJ props were kind of a bluish, but the ANH ones look more grey. What's right?
		

Click to expand...

Hey, that's my buildup!  Cool someone found it useful.

What you're seeing is a trick of the light, the miniatures look much lighter under the harsh shooting lights.  Pics of the models at various museums, depending on what film they were used for, register two colors, the light, cold grey or the blue tint of ESB and ROTJ.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #1070  (forum post #940058)
Author    : GKvfx
Date      : Jul 23, 2009 at 3:11 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I've attached the files that I posted over on the RI.  I can't find the originals I made - if you can't read the tiny text I used on the photos - go to the RI thread here - http://www.resinilluminati.com/showpost.php?p=120852&postcount=7

But to summarize, the basic answer, apparently, is a blue-gray.  And fairly dark, too.  I was surprised as well.  In talking to some people about Edlund's damaged TIE we concluded:

- That it was an original Ep.IV model.

- It hadn't been messed with (ie: wings, body parts swapped out) save      for the replacing of the top hatch cover (which was an ILM casting).

- Likely is more "original" than the ones on display with the tours which we've seen, at times, to have ROTJ bodies with ESB wings.

And since the paint on the damaged top hatch that I replaced on Edlund's TIE matches the rest of the paint on the ship, that tells me that the paint on the hatch IS what they used on Ep. IV.

And, having photographed Edlund's TIE before it went out, I can tell you how different it looks on (digital) film and in person.  Once you get a lot of light on the model, it really starts to loose color and go to a light gray.  And the optical process, as has been pointed out, exacerbates the difference.

Sooooo, like the original TV Enterprise, it boils down to painting it either the way it was sitting on stage, or the way you remember seeing it on screen.  I'll argue that it's a matter of personal preference.

Gene

Heard from Steve last night- he's had a lot on his plate and been gone for work duties; it sound like he has been using his weekend to continue chipping away at orders, including shipping out my Starfighters.

I've been in the same boat as Steve with getting out garage kits- a work situation cropps up and suddenly you aren't in charge of our own time- and that includes time to even get to some computer terminal to communicate with customers.  

Not that it won't be frustrating to anyone on the other end, but it seems to be the nature of th GK industry.  I've been on all ends of this (kit maker, trade and cash customer) and if you have to boil it down to one statement, it's that this stuff just happens.  Maybe its not a good excuse, but that just the facts.

If you approach this with the idea that Steve is not out to rip anybody off (and I have NO doubt about this), then perhaps it will make the delays easier to take.

Just my 2 cents...

Mark

Post #1137  (forum post #974327)
Author    : vaderdarth
Date      : Sep 2, 2009 at 1:12 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Sorry if I sounded irate Jason,  it just seemed odd that I've seen the same guys dogpiling Steve in different threads and even on other boards I've visited.  

I'm really only the messenger and not a go between for Steve, so I wouldn't call myself his liason.  What he does is his business.  I am his friend on the other hand,  and I speak with the guy every couple days about totally unrelated issues.  

I know that Steve doesn't wish any of you three any ill will.  Nobody feels worse about being behind schedule than the guy that's behind schedule.   Steve promised he wouldn't do any mass runs and he's kept his word on that to catch up on back logs.  I happen to know his back log is progressing at a rate of about 4 kits less each week.  I think that is more than reasonable to expect.  Any more would create shoddy kits.   Nobody wants that.  

I have spoken to at least 3 guys who've already received their kits and they are all extremely happy with the quality of the castings (no suprise there!) and a couple have said the end results justified the wait time.  

Steve does not deny he has fallen behind but the simple fact is this gentlemen:  with garage kits,  the only way to make product before taking money is to be independently wealthy.  

Nobody in the garage kit trade,   takes orders with the intent to not be able to follow thru as originally intended.    Nobody would do that to themselves or their customers.    What happens is a guy sets a time line based on what he can normally produce,  takes funds,  and then life has a way of destroying his time line without his consent.  Then it leads to delays and disappointment.    

I'm waiting on a kit myself but these other guys are ahead of me in the backlog.  I've known Steve long enough to know he's making good on this stuff.  He needed funds for shipping for at least 3 kits sitting by his door and that money was owed to him by myself for an unrelated project.  I was a week late making that payment to him.  So two guys kits sat by the door until today.    Unless you are Richie Rich,  you have to rob Peter to pay Paul occasionally.   Usually things go fine until just one guy comes along and wants a refund,   then you have to relinquish some of your resin money to give him his money back,   Now where does your resin money come from?   

Here's another scenario,  you are on schedule and a guy claims his kit didn't arrive that you have the tracking info proving you shipped.   You have to replace this guys kit now and he's priority,   so you take some other guys kit to replace the shortage.  Then where does that resin money come from.  Good luck getting it from the US Postal Service.  

Let's not even get into the personal issues Steve and other guys have had to face.  How do you pump out 3-4 kits when your whole weekend gets stolen by a family illness or a work schedule change???

They call these things garage kits because these guys are hobbyists who make these cool toys in their own homes.  

Steve is working on a couple issues with his time management where these kits are concerned.  He's getting physical help on both pouring parts,  trimming parts and then help on boxing and shipping.    He knows he needs to build alot more leeway for "real life" into things before he starts new projects.  

I don't think we can ask much more of the guy.  

Jason,  I love the avatar!   
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Dave

If I may, though:

vaderdarth said:

			... the simple fact is this gentlemen:  with garage kits,  the only way to make product before taking money is to be independently wealthy.
		

Click to expand...

I'm FAR from independently wealthy, but I can pull it off. You start small, keep your GK money separate from living expenses and spending money, and grow it slowly over the years - dumping everything back into the next project. Heck, you can even claim it on your taxes and pay taxes on the profits, AND claim all the expenses. If/when a kit bombs and you take a loss, you get $$ back in your refund!

This kit took 2 years and about $2,000 in donor kits to make, and I paid for waterslide decals - I farmed out the castings so I pay a lot more for resin/rubber/labor, but I get the kits professionally flawlessly cast and pre-packed.

http://www.mystery10.com/

It took me 4 years to get to this level of kit sales though - started out selling buttons, t-shirts and little baby resin kits.

It can be done right, by poor people, honest!
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #1139  (forum post #974340)
Author    : vaderdarth
Date      : Sep 2, 2009 at 1:27 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Good advise Jason and I'm sure Steve will be listening to lots of advise on how to streamline everything.  

I am beginning to get into the garage kits as well and I'm keeping my goal of literally not taking money before I have product to ship.  Now having said that,  I am a dentist and I had to sink at least 5K into my projects prior to asking for a single dime.  If I worked down at the carwash,  there is no possible way I could do this.  

Some of the very best GK folks out there ask for funds up front in the way of pre-orders.   They don't set any time lines whatsoever.   The pre-order thing is simply a way of generating operating costs up front,  plus a pre-order saves the customer about 50 bucks per kit as the regular price is always higher if people wait til it's finished.  So Pre-orders begin with a photo of what is to come...............then the research/development phase and finally the finished model.   Most projects take 6 months start to finish in cases like this.  

I commend you Jason on your business model and hope it always goes according to plan for you.  Everyone just isn't so fortunate.  

Steve knows that getting key help for both production and packaging is the road to success and I know he's working on that.  
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Guys I'm pretty confident that all remaining backorders aside from the Y wings are going to be shipped pretty shortly.  Steve's been super busy but that was the general plan in our last two conversations.  If he gets time I'll post the list of the latest shipments.  Once the last known backlog orders are shipped,  I will have a special price on 3 of the older version TIE standard kits which are ready to ship.  Since they are the older body style,  The price is gonna be pretty fantastic.  These are what is left since everyone who ordered got upgraded to the newer two piece body style.   I'll post more info soon.  I'll be following that up with an interest list for those wanting either a Standard, Hero or Interceptor TIE.   Those will be sold in mixed lots of 5 kits.   I will first create an interest list and see who wants what,  then Steve will make the 5 kits,  then once they are boxed and ready to roll out,  I'll accept payment.   From now on,  this is how it will work.   Nobody pays and waits,  no payments until the kits are ready.  

Dave

Paul Heaberlin said:

			Here's to hoping it's just a cockpit upgrade instead of an entire head replacement
		

Click to expand...

 

The cockpit upgrade/insert will only work with the new cockpit. The cockpit itself has been made larger. I don't know to what extent exactly John is going too.

 It will ultimately comprise of 5 parts, upper and lower hull, cockpit insert (accurate to the heroes), the canopy and firewall. Yes in essence it will be hollow.  Two distinct panel detailing (red or gold) will be offered.  

A rod (mounting point) will traverse the model incorporating the cockpit itself.   

Much more to come

Post #1269  (forum post #1032846)
Author    : vaderdarth
Date      : Nov 10, 2009 at 6:11 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I do prefer PMs as some of the boards emails get screened out as spam for some reason.  Probably a hotmail thing.  

I want to keep it in PMs as that way I can keep everyone together.  Most of my messages come thru PMs anyway. 

No list yet on the Ywings.   Both versions have now been upgraded so I probably won't have prices until they hit rubber etc...  

I have asked Steve for an update on pricing for future stuff so just hang tight for the moment.  I know everyone  wants to know early so they can start stashing their coins away.  I'm in the same boat.  It's hard to know what a kit will cost until you see what it costs to mould and reproduce it.  

Once the last couple backlog orders leave Steve's hands.   I will start an interest only thread.  It will have pricing and details so folks can see what each style will cost.  Metal Armature upgrades will be at least $100 over the kit cost.  

Don't forget.  When we do start a for sale thread,  we will only be selling what is on hand.  So you can't order, for example,  a metal armature if he doesn't have one on hand.  You'll simply have to wait on the metal armature for sale thread.  I know that sux,  but we ain't gonna be staring at backlogs anymore.  
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Dave

"next time"  man i cant wait for that to show how we are going to do things different.  Once a collector pays the kit ships  the next day as the kit would be "on hand"  no more pre orders... no more taking hard earned money when the kit is NOT ready!  Period end of story!

Ive benn working hard and not taking new orders...  Ive paid for most of this past two month shipping on my own.. I know it my own fault but I think its helped me learn a hard lesson...   

listen up garage kit producers..

Here it comes.....

#1 RULE:  DO NOT TAKE MONEY FROM A CUSTOMER UNTIL THE PRODUCT IS READY TO SHIP.  

pretty simple.  Everyone is happy in the end! 2010 is looking to be my best year yet!

Steve

Post #1389  (forum post #1149567)
Author    : vaderdarth
Date      : Mar 5, 2010 at 8:11 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I believe the plan for future kits is to have a visual parts sheet which shows every part in the entire kit,  by which the actual kit you receive has been crosschecked against prior to closing up the box.  Does that make sense?  This new  process will eliminate any missing kit parts. We can physically make a photocopy of the parts stuck onto a sheet of paper,  then take the plastic pieces,  sit them onto the photocopy and make sure each item has a physical part in place,  before bagging and boxing the item.  When you have so many parts it is often easy to overlook a piece here or there,  but in this way nothing gets left out.  

Dave 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Post #1540  (forum post #1883665)
Author    : vaderdarth
Date      : Sep 12, 2011 at 1:32 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

When I built the first TIE kit,  I put the stars on the belt sander and thinned them down and they fit the armature fine for me.  There is still thickness to the koolshade and cardstock inside.  So keep that in mind.  Put all your layers together before you cut down that armature.  You only get one shot at it.  
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Post #1542  (forum post #1884239)
Author    : moffeaton
Date      : Sep 12, 2011 at 5:55 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Here we go - here you see one wingstar in position (with the extra armature passing through), and then the second one nested behind it - see how much armature is STILL sticking past? Sadly, these two wingstars when together are THICKER that .25", which is the ANH wing thickness. So there will be at least this much extra armature to contend with.

[IMAGE: tieex1.jpg]

Here you see the 1/4" Plastruct H-Beam edge thickness roughly correlates to this delineation in the resin wingstar that clearly shows that the master was the correct thickness at some point (look at the red line). Below that, I show how both wingstars when nested together (as shown above) are still thicker than the .25" H-Beam (red lines delineate the wingstars thickness). These stars should sandwich two layers of Kool Shade (and that construction paper) and be level with the H-Beam, as ANH TIE pictures clearly illustrate.

[IMAGE: tieex2.jpg]

So yeah - this is gonna be rough to get looking correct to ANH specs.

Post #1549  (forum post #1885424)
Author    : moffeaton
Date      : Sep 13, 2011 at 7:40 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I think a solution is in hand for this - a jig and an aluminum cutter. It's an unnecessary headache, though, isn't it? A little more care and attention and this woudl not happen. I know a resin garage kit requires extra elbow grease, but it infuriates me when you have to do extra work for no other reason than someone was asleep at the wheel. That's not a fault of lack of reference, or other understandable things - it's just sloppiness. It's lame. I'm not blaming Steve, either - for all I know, one of his helpers shipped this one to my client. Impossible to tell.

"TBH I'm nore concerned about the thickness of the stars themselves."

It goes like this: < wing star - kool shade - paper - kool shade - wing star>

The 1/4" Plastruct H-Beam dictates the thickness - Gene's pics prove this. 

The <kool shade - paper - kool shade> should socket into the H-Beam, and the wing star on each side should mate up perfectly with the other H'Beam surfaces. 

So the wing stars should be really really thin - as thin as the protruding bits of the "H". (technically that H is on it's side, like a capital I)

Crop from Gene's pic posted elsewhere:

[IMAGE: TIE-006.jpg]

Post #1560  (forum post #1886079)
Author    : vaderdarth
Date      : Sep 13, 2011 at 1:10 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

There is a trim line on the wing stars.  You sand them down to that trim line.  If you poured them that thin,  they'd be too brittle to ship as big and lanky as they are.   It takes a bit of work,  but a belt sander does the trick.   I keep saying I want to build one of those vibrating sanding jigs with the holes in it attached to a vacuum hose to catch the dust..............I'm too lazy to follow through.

PS the black matte art board is about 1mm thick,  it is rigid and will help hold the shape, especially once the koolshade is glued down onto it.  

the wing shape is cut out of the art board.  The wedges of koolshade go down with the ends touching the ends of the other pieces.  Then the stars already painted are epoxied down onto the koolshade all the way to the corners of the wings for ANH,  But only to the beginning of the outer wing trim for ESB/ROTJ

Dave
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #1578  (forum post #1907151)
Author    : moffeaton
Date      : Sep 22, 2011 at 7:55 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Ahhh using those thick stunt wings. Glad it works for you. But I'm shooting for accurate ANH wings, built with real Kool Shade, they need to be WAY thinner, and the armature is therefore WAY too long, especially at 14". I must be in the minority - it's making more sense now, after seeing your pic. The armatures were tailored to those stunt wings.

Real untouched ANH TIE wing is .25" at the leading edge, including the wing star strut thickness (see how thin it's supposed to be? But it's funny to see how one star is thicker than the other, heh)... even adding the "hub plate" thickness, you're still going to be way thinner:

[IMAGE: IMG_1471.jpg]

realize this is not canon, but a simply engineering fix (if i was there from initial design)? -- instead of one rod (wing-to-wing) have two outer rods, then the inner piece is a pipe, where the two outer rods fit into.  adjust the length as you need, then tighten the rod to pipe connection.

Post #1592  (forum post #1939255)
Author    : vaderdarth
Date      : Oct 9, 2011 at 7:26 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Well I did end up cutting the armature.  It was easy enough.  Took about 15 min.  I used a rotozip cutoff wheel and then sanded smooth with a belt sander.  Easy peasy.  

All future kits will have a cast resin armature with metal reinforcement.  This should eliminate these issues.   

I also suggest using a belt sander for reducing the thickness of the wing stars.  This step will remove all the flash so don't try to do that first as it's not necessary.  Thin the hubs first then do the short arms of the stars,  then the long arms.  I reduced until mine were about 2mm.  This is pretty close to the screen models.  

I'm going to do a photo tutorial for the hero wing assembly soon.   I've been snapping pix and will try to assemble the info into a step by step.  

Dave 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
